    35	proc wait_for_role {srv_idx role} {
    36	    # Wait for the role, make sure the replication role matches.
    37	    wait_for_condition 100 100 {
    38	        [lindex [split [R $srv_idx ROLE] " "] 0] eq $role
    39	    } else {
    40	        puts "R $srv_idx ROLE: [R $srv_idx ROLE]"
    41	        fail "R $srv_idx didn't assume the replication $role in time"
    42	    }
    43	
    44	    if {$role eq "slave"} {
    45	        # Wait for the replication link, make sure the replication link is normal.
    46	        wait_for_condition 100 100 {
    47	            [s -$srv_idx master_link_status] eq "up"
    48	        } else {
    49	            puts "R $srv_idx INFO REPLICATION: [R $srv_idx INFO REPLICATION]"
    50	            fail "R $srv_idx didn't assume the replication link in time"
    51	        }
    52	    }
    53	
    54	    # Wait for the cluster role, make sure the cluster role matches.
    55	    wait_for_condition 100 100 {
    56	        [get_cluster_role $srv_idx] eq $role
    57	    } else {
    58	        puts "R $srv_idx CLUSTER NODES: [R $srv_idx CLUSTER NODES]"
    59	        fail "R $srv_idx didn't assume the cluster $role in time"
    60	    }

    62	    if {$role eq "slave"} {
    63	        # Wait for the flags, make sure the primary node is not failed.
    64	        wait_for_condition 100 100 {
    65	            [get_myself_primary_flags $srv_idx] eq "master"
    66	        } else {
    67	            puts "R $srv_idx CLUSTER NODES: [R $srv_idx CLUSTER NODES]"
    68	            fail "R $srv_idx didn't assume the primary state in time"

    74	        } else {

    91	# restart a server and wait for it to come back online
    92	proc fail_server {server_id} {
    93	    set node_timeout [lindex [R 0 CONFIG GET cluster-node-timeout] 1]
    94	    pause_process [srv [expr -1*$server_id] pid]
    95	    after [expr 3*$node_timeout]
    96	    resume_process [srv [expr -1*$server_id] pid]
    97	}

    99	proc migrate_slot {from to slot} {
   100	    set from_id [R $from CLUSTER MYID]
   101	    set to_id [R $to CLUSTER MYID]
   102	    assert_equal {OK} [R $from CLUSTER SETSLOT $slot MIGRATING $to_id]
   103	    assert_equal {OK} [R $to CLUSTER SETSLOT $slot IMPORTING $from_id]
   104	}

   118	        # Validate initial states
   119	        assert_not_equal [get_open_slots 0] "\[609->-$R1_id\]"
   120	        assert_not_equal [get_open_slots 1] "\[609-<-$R0_id\]"
   121	        assert_not_equal [get_open_slots 3] "\[609->-$R1_id\]"
   122	        assert_not_equal [get_open_slots 4] "\[609-<-$R0_id\]"
   123	        # Kick off the migration of slot 609 from R0 to R1
   124	        assert_equal {OK} [R 0 CLUSTER SETSLOT 609 MIGRATING $R1_id]
   125	        assert_equal {OK} [R 1 CLUSTER SETSLOT 609 IMPORTING $R0_id]
   126	        # Validate that R0 is migrating slot 609 to R1
   127	        assert_equal [get_open_slots 0] "\[609->-$R1_id\]"
   128	        # Validate that R1 is importing slot 609 from R0

   260	proc create_empty_shard {p r} {
   261	    set node_timeout [lindex [R 0 CONFIG GET cluster-node-timeout] 1]
   262	    assert_equal {OK} [R $p CLUSTER RESET]
   263	    assert_equal {OK} [R $r CLUSTER RESET]
   264	    assert_equal {OK} [R $p CLUSTER MEET [srv 0 "host"] [srv 0 "port"]]
   265	    assert_equal {OK} [R $r CLUSTER MEET [srv 0 "host"] [srv 0 "port"]]
   266	    wait_for_role $p master
   267	    assert_equal {OK} [R $r CLUSTER REPLICATE [R $p CLUSTER MYID]]
   268	    wait_for_role $r slave
   269	    wait_for_role $p master
   270	}

  2818	                     * Nevertheless, there are scenarios where the source shard may have transferred slot
  2819	                     * to a different shard. In these cases, the bumping of the config epoch
  2820	                     * could result in that slot assignment getting reverted. However, we consider
  2821	                     * this as a very rare case and err on the side of being consistent with the current
  2822	                     * practice. */
  2823	                    clusterDelSlot(j);
  2824	                    clusterAddSlot(myself, j);
  2825	                    clusterBumpConfigEpochWithoutConsensus();
  2826	                    clusterDoBeforeSleep(CLUSTER_TODO_SAVE_CONFIG | CLUSTER_TODO_UPDATE_STATE |
  2827	                                         CLUSTER_TODO_FSYNC_CONFIG);
  2828	                }
  2829	            }
  2830	        }
  2831	    }
  2832	
  2833	    /* After updating the slots configuration, don't do any actual change
  2834	     * in the state of the server if a module disabled Cluster
  2835	     * keys redirections. */
  2836	    if (server.cluster_module_flags & CLUSTER_MODULE_FLAG_NO_REDIRECTION) return;
  2837	
  2838	    /* Handle a special case where new_primary is not set but both sender
  2839	     * and myself own no slots and in the same shard. Set the sender as
  2840	     * the new primary if my current config epoch is lower than the
  2841	     * sender's. */
  2842	    if (!new_primary && myself->replicaof != sender && sender_slots == 0 && myself->numslots == 0 &&
  2843	        nodeEpoch(myself) < senderConfigEpoch && are_in_same_shard) {
  2844	        new_primary = sender;
  2845	    }
  2846	
  2847	    /* If the shard to which this node (myself) belongs loses all of
  2848	     * its slots, this node should become a replica of the sender if
  2849	     * one of the following conditions is true:
  2850	     *

2026-05-28 18:39:43,030 - DEBUG - swea-tools - Retrieved state from environment: {'working_dir': '/testbed'}
2026-05-28 18:39:43,034 - INFO - swea-agent - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:
commit 507042df9642a0f70f991d87003ffaab2246ceea
Author: Binbin <binloveplay1314@qq.com>
Date:   Fri Jul 11 19:00:16 2025 +0800

    Fix replica (the old primary) claims to sitll have slots after manual failover (#2301)
    
    After a failover occurs, when the PING-PONG of the replica, that is,
    the old primary, reaches other shard nodes faster, the corresponding
    code path will be reached. We will adjust the sender to be a replica
    and sender_claimed_primary to be the primary node, but in myself view,
    slots still belong to the sender, which is a replica.
    
    This actually restores part of the code in 28976a9003c6dd5cdd7225c5bc90743b4fcde13c.
    It was lost in the changes to #445 and #754.
    
    These 3 changes are about avoiding the replicaof cycle but ended up creating
    a "cycle" of assumptions themselves. when #445 removed this logic, it was
    assumed that a replica could also drive clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith
    but this was actually a regression that resulted in a replicaof cycle (#753).
    #754 fixed the replicaof cycle by disallowing a replica to drive
    clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith but missed restoring the original logic.
    
    Added a new `DEBUG DISABLE-CLUSTER-RECONNECTION <0|1>` this will prevent
    cluster nodes from reconnecting so that the issue can be reproduce in test.
    
    Signed-off-by: Binbin <binloveplay1314@qq.com>
    Co-authored-by: Ping Xie <pingxie@outlook.com>

+/* Transfer slots from `from_node` to `to_node`.
+ *
+ * Iterates over all cluster slots, transferring each slot covered
+ * by `from_node` to `to_node`. Counts and returns the number of
+ * slots transferred. */
+int clusterMoveNodeSlots(clusterNode *from_node, clusterNode *to_node) {
+    int processed = 0;
+    for (int j = 0; j < CLUSTER_SLOTS; j++) {
+        if (clusterNodeCoversSlot(from_node, j)) {
+            clusterDelSlot(j);
+            clusterAddSlot(to_node, j);
+            processed++;
+        }
+    }
+    return processed;
+}

+start_cluster 3 1 {tags {external:skip cluster}} {
+    # In the R0/R3 shard, R0 is the primary node and R3 is the replica.
+    #
+    # We trigger a manually failover on R3.
+    #
+    # When R3 becomes the new primary node, it will broadcast a message to all
+    # nodes in the cluster.
+    # When R0 receives the message, it becomes the new replica and also will
+    # broadcast the message to all nodes in the cluster.
+    #
+    # Let's assume that R1 and R2 receive the message from R0 (new replica) first
+    # and then the message from R3 (new primary) later.
+    #
+    # The purpose of this test is to verify the behavior of R1 and R2 after receiving
+    # the message from R0 (new replica) first. R1 and R2 will update R0 as a replica
+    # and R3 as a primary, and transfer all slots of R0 to R3.
+    test "The role change and the slot ownership change should be an atomic operation" {
+        set R0_nodeid [R 0 cluster myid]
+        set R1_nodeid [R 1 cluster myid]
+        set R2_nodeid [R 2 cluster myid]
+        set R3_nodeid [R 3 cluster myid]
+
+        set R0_shardid [R 0 cluster myshardid]
+        set R3_shardid [R 3 cluster myshardid]
+        assert_equal $R0_shardid $R3_shardid
+
+        # Ensure that related nodes do not reconnect.
+        R 1 debug disable-cluster-reconnection 1
+        R 2 debug disable-cluster-reconnection 1
+        R 3 debug disable-cluster-reconnection 1
+
+        # After killing the cluster link, ensure that R1 and R2 do not receive
+        # messages from R3 (new primary).
+        R 1 debug clusterlink kill all $R3_nodeid
+        R 2 debug clusterlink kill all $R3_nodeid
+        R 3 debug clusterlink kill all $R1_nodeid
+        R 3 debug clusterlink kill all $R2_nodeid
+
+        set loglines1 [count_log_lines -1]
+        set loglines2 [count_log_lines -2]
+
+        R 3 cluster failover takeover
+
+        # Check that from the perspectives of R1 and R2, R0 becomes a replica and
+        # R3 becomes the new primary.
+        wait_for_condition 1000 10 {
+            [cluster_has_flag [cluster_get_node_by_id 1 $R0_nodeid] slave] eq 1 &&
+            [cluster_has_flag [cluster_get_node_by_id 1 $R3_nodeid] master] eq 1 &&
+
+            [cluster_has_flag [cluster_get_node_by_id 2 $R0_nodeid] slave] eq 1 &&
+            [cluster_has_flag [cluster_get_node_by_id 2 $R3_nodeid] master] eq 1
+        } else {
+            fail "The node is not marked with the correct flag"
+        }
+
+        # Check that R0 (replica) does not own any slots and R3 (new primary) owns
+        # the slots.
+        assert_equal {} [dict get [cluster_get_node_by_id 1 $R0_nodeid] slots]
+        assert_equal {} [dict get [cluster_get_node_by_id 2 $R0_nodeid] slots]
+        assert_equal {0-5461} [dict get [cluster_get_node_by_id 1 $R3_nodeid] slots]
+        assert_equal {0-5461} [dict get [cluster_get_node_by_id 2 $R3_nodeid] slots]
+
+        # A failover occurred in shard, we will only go to this code branch,
+        # verify we print the logs.
+        set R0_slots 5462
+        set pattern "*A failover occurred in shard $R3_shardid; node $R0_nodeid () lost $R0_slots slot(s) and failed over to node $R3_nodeid*"
+        verify_log_message -1 $pattern $loglines1
+        verify_log_message -2 $pattern $loglines2
+
+        R 1 debug disable-cluster-reconnection 0
+        R 2 debug disable-cluster-reconnection 0
+        R 3 debug disable-cluster-reconnection 0
+
+        wait_for_cluster_propagation
+    }
+}

  5819	            processed++;
  5820	        }
  5821	    }
  5822	    return processed;
  5823	}
  5824	
  5825	/* Clear the migrating / importing state for all the slots.
  5826	 * This is useful at initialization and when turning a primary into replica. */

*** Migration source is auto-updated after failover in source shard

Let me look at the test again:

```tcl
test "Migration source is auto-updated after failover in source shard" {
    # Trigger an auto-failover from R0 to R3
    fail_server 0
    # Wait for R0 to become a replica
    wait_for_role 0 slave
    # Validate final states
    wait_for_slot_state 0 "\[609->-$R1_id\]"
    wait_for_slot_state 1 "\[609-<-$R3_id\]"

    wait_for_slot_state 4 "\[609-<-$R3_id\]"
    ...
}
```

So the test expects that after failover in source shard (R0 -> R3):
- R0 (now replica) still shows migrating state (609->-$R1_id)
- R1 (target) shows importing from R3 (609-<-$R3_id)
- R3 (new primary) shows migrating state (609->-$R1_id)
- R4 (replica of R1) shows importing from R3 (609-<-$R3_id)

The key issue is that when slots are moved from R0 to R3 via `clusterMoveNodeSlots`, the migrating state for the slot might get lost because:
1. R0's slots are moved to R3
2. But `server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[slot]` for R0's slots might not be properly transferred

Now I understand the flow better. In `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith`, when the sender claims a slot that was previously owned by someone else and the sender has a higher configEpoch:

1. It checks if there's a `migrating_slots_to[j]` - if the new owner is not in the same shard, it clears the migrating state. If in the same shard, it retains it.
2. It checks if there's an `importing_slots_from[j]` - if the new owner (sender) is in the same shard as the old importing source, it updates the importing source to sender. Otherwise, it clears it.

Now, the problem with PR #2301 is: when the old primary (sender) sends a PONG saying it's now a replica, the code at line 3666-3682 moves slots from the old primary to the new primary via `clusterMoveNodeSlots`. But this bypasses the normal `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` logic that properly handles migrating/importing states!

Specifically, `clusterMoveNodeSlots` just does `clusterDelSlot(j)` and `clusterAddSlot(to_node, j)` without any of the migration state updates that `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` does.

But wait - later when the new primary sends its PING, `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` will be called. At that point, the slot already belongs to the new primary (because `clusterMoveNodeSlots` already moved it). So the condition at line 2685 (`server.cluster->slots[j] == sender`) will be true, and it will just `continue` without doing any migration state updates!

That's the bug! When `clusterMoveNodeSlots` is called first (from the old primary's PONG), the slots are moved to the new primary. Then when the new primary's PING arrives and `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` is called, the slots already belong to the sender (new primary), so the migration state updates are skipped entirely.

Let me verify this by looking more at the condition on line 2685:

```c
/* The slot is already bound to the sender of this message. */
if (server.cluster->slots[j] == sender) {
    bitmapClearBit(server.cluster->owner_not_claiming_slot, j);
    continue;
}
```

Yes! If the slot already belongs to the sender, it just clears the `owner_not_claiming_slot` bit and continues. The migration state updates (lines 2715-2752) are only done when the slot is being reassigned from someone else to the sender (the `else` branch starting at line 2693).

So the fix should be in `clusterMoveNodeSlots` or in the code that calls it. The migration states should be properly handled when slots are moved.

Let me think about what the correct behavior should be:

When slots are moved from `from_node` (old primary) to `to_node` (new primary) due to a failover in the same shard:
1. For migrating slots: `migrating_slots_to[slot]` should remain pointing to the same target (since the migration target doesn't change). But the slot owner changed from `from_node` to `to_node`.
2. For importing slots: `importing_slots_from[slot]` should be updated to point to `to_node` (the new primary) instead of `from_node` (the old primary), since they're in the same shard.

But wait, `clusterMoveNodeSlots` operates on the observer node's state. The observer might have its own `migrating_slots_to` and `importing_slots_from` arrays. Let me check if the observer's migration states are relevant.

Actually, looking at the code, `migrating_slots_to` and `importing_slots_from` are local to each node. They represent the migration state from this node's perspective. So when an observer node sees a failover in a source shard, it should update its `importing_slots_from` if it was importing from the old primary.

But actually, the observer node might not be importing/migrating anything. The migration states are only set on the nodes directly involved in migration. However, the tests check that replicas also show the migration states (via `cluster slots` or `cluster nodes`). Let me check how replicas get the migration state.

Let me look at how the slot info is propagated to replicas and how `get_open_slots` works.

Looking at the test helper:
```tcl
proc get_open_slots {srv_idx} {
    set slots [dict get [cluster_get_myself $srv_idx] slots]
    ...
}
```

This gets the slots information from `CLUSTER NODES` output for a specific server. The migration states are shown in the slot information.

Now, the issue might be that when a node receives the PONG from the old primary (now replica) and moves slots via `clusterMoveNodeSlots`, the migration/importing states are not updated. But later, when the new primary's PING is processed, the slots already belong to the new primary, so the migration state updates in `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` are skipped.

Let me look at `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` more carefully. The logic at lines 2721-2752 handles migration states. But this code only runs when the slot is being reassigned (lines 2693-2757). If the slot already belongs to sender (line 2685), it just continues.

So the fix should be to also handle migration states when the slot already belongs to the sender but there are pending migration states that need updating. OR, the fix should be in `clusterMoveNodeSlots` to properly update migration states.

Wait, let me reconsider. Let me look at what happens when `clusterMoveNodeSlots` is called. In the scenario:

1. R0 is primary, migrating slot 609 to R1 (target). So R0 has `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`.
2. R1 is primary, importing slot 609 from R0. So R1 has `importing_slots_from[609] = R0`.
3. R0 fails, R3 takes over as new primary in the same shard.
4. R0 (now replica) sends a PONG to other nodes announcing it's a replica.
5. Other nodes (like R1, R2, R4, R5) receive this PONG. They call `clusterMoveNodeSlots(R0, R3)` which moves slot 609 from R0 to R3.
6. But the migration states on these observer nodes are still pointing to R0 or R1.

Now, the observer nodes aren't directly involved in the migration (they're not R0 or R1). But wait, the test checks `get_open_slots` on R0, R1, R3, R4. These are the nodes themselves:
- R0 is the old primary (now replica)
- R1 is the target primary
- R3 is the new primary in source shard
- R4 is the replica of R1

So the migration states on R1 (target) are important. R1 has `importing_slots_from[609] = R0`. When R1 receives the PONG from R0 (now replica), it will move slot 609 from R0 to R3 via `clusterMoveNodeSlots`. But `importing_slots_from[609]` still points to R0 (the old primary). It should now point to R3 (the new primary).

Then when R3's PING arrives at R1, `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith(R3, ...)` is called. Since slot 609 already belongs to R3 (moved by `clusterMoveNodeSlots`), the condition at line 2685 is true and it just continues without updating `importing_slots_from[609]`.

So the bug is: `importing_slots_from[609]` still points to R0, but it should point to R3.

Similarly for `migrating_slots_to`: R0 has `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`. When R0 becomes a replica and its slots are moved to R3, the migrating state on R3 (which is now the slot owner) should be `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`. But `clusterMoveNodeSlots` doesn't propagate this.

2. `migrating_slots_to[slot]` should remain unchanged (it points to the migration target, which hasn't changed).

But also, what about the case where the observer node itself has `migrating_slots_to[slot]` pointing to `sender`? That would mean the observer is migrating a slot to the old primary. Since the old primary is now a replica, the migration should be updated to point to the new primary in the same shard.

Wait, actually, looking at the `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` logic at lines 2775-2784:

```c
if (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] != NULL && server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] != sender &&
    (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j]->configEpoch < senderConfigEpoch ||
     nodeIsReplica(server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j])) &&
    areInSameShard(server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j], sender)) {
    ...
    server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] = sender;
}
```

This updates `migrating_slots_to[j]` when the migration target (the node we're migrating to) has a failover - it updates to point to the sender (new primary in the target shard). This code runs in the `else` branch (when the sender does NOT claim the slot). But in our case, the sender (new primary) DOES claim the slot, so this code path wouldn't be reached.

I think the cleanest fix is to update `clusterMoveNodeSlots` to also update the migration/importing states. Or, alternatively, to not use `clusterMoveNodeSlots` at all and instead let `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` handle the slot movement properly (by not moving slots prematurely).

But wait, the purpose of PR #2301 was to fix a specific issue: "Fix replica (the old primary) claims to still have slots after manual failover". The issue is that after a failover, the old primary's PONG reaches other nodes first, and they see the old primary as still having slots. The fix moves the slots to the new primary immediately when they learn about the failover.

The problem is that this slot movement skips the migration state updates.

Let me write a fix that updates migration states in `clusterMoveNodeSlots` or in the calling code.

Actually, looking more carefully, I think the fix should be in the block that calls `clusterMoveNodeSlots`. After moving slots, we should iterate through the moved slots and update migration states:

```c
int slots = clusterMoveNodeSlots(sender, sender_claimed_primary);
/* Update migration states for the moved slots */
for (int j = 0; j < CLUSTER_SLOTS; j++) {
    if (server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j] == sender) {
        server.cluster->importing_slots_from[j] = sender_claimed_primary;
    }
    if (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] == sender) {
        server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] = sender_claimed_primary;
    }
}
```

But wait, should `migrating_slots_to[j]` be updated? If `migrating_slots_to[j]` points to `sender` (old primary), it means the observer node is migrating slot `j` TO the old primary. Now that the old primary is a replica, the migration should be redirected to the new primary in the same shard. That seems correct.

However, I also need to consider: what if the observer node is the migration target? For example, R1 is importing slot 609 from R0. R1 has `importing_slots_from[609] = R0`. When R1 receives the PONG from R0 (old primary), it calls `clusterMoveNodeSlots(R0, R3)` which moves slot 609 from R0 to R3. Then we update `importing_slots_from[609]` from R0 to R3. That's correct.

But also, what if the observer node has `migrating_slots_to[609]` pointing to R1? That would be on R0 itself (or its new primary R3). But R0 is the one that became a replica, and its own migration states are handled differently (through `clusterSetPrimary` which doesn't call `clusterCloseAllSlots` if same shard). So R0 retains its `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`. That's fine.

But what about R3 (the new primary)? R3 might not have been aware of the migration before the failover. After the failover, R3 should inherit the migration state. But does R3 receive the PONG from R0? R3 is in the same shard as R0, so R3 should receive R0's PONG. When R3 processes R0's PONG, it will call `clusterMoveNodeSlots(R0, R3)` but wait - R3 is `sender_claimed_primary`. Actually, R3 is both the sender_claimed_primary and the observer. Let me check: does the code at line 3666 run on R3 itself?

Looking at line 3666:
```c
} else if (nodeIsReplica(sender_claimed_primary)) {
```

For R3, `sender_claimed_primary` would be R3 itself (since R0 claims R3 as its primary). But `nodeIsReplica(R3)` would be false (R3 is the new primary). So this code path would NOT be taken on R3. Instead, R3 would go to the `else` branch at line 3684? No wait, let me check the conditions:

- `sender` = R0 (old primary, now replica)
- `sender_claimed_primary` = R3 (new primary)
- `areInSameShard(sender_claimed_primary, sender)` = true (same shard)
- `nodeEpoch(sender_claimed_primary) > sender_claimed_config_epoch`? 
- `nodeIsReplica(sender_claimed_primary)`? For R3, R3 is the new primary, so `nodeIsReplica(R3)` should be... let me check. On R3 itself, after the failover, R3 is now primary. But when R3 receives the PONG from R0, R3 might still view itself as replica? Actually, R3 initiated the failover and became primary, so it should view itself as primary.

Wait, but this code is about the observer node's view of `sender_claimed_primary`. If the observer is R3 itself, then `sender_claimed_primary` = R3. In R3's own view, is R3 a replica? If R3 already became primary (since it won the failover), then `nodeIsReplica(R3)` is false. So the code at line 3666-3682 is NOT executed on R3. Instead, what happens on R3?

Let me look at what happens when R3 receives R0's PONG. R3 is the new primary. The condition at line 3654:
```c
if (sender_claimed_primary && areInSameShard(sender_claimed_primary, sender)) {
```
This is true (R3 is in the same shard as R0).

Then:
```c
if (nodeEpoch(sender_claimed_primary) > sender_claimed_config_epoch) {
```
This checks if R3's epoch is greater than what R0 claims. If R3 already has a higher epoch (which it should after winning failover), this returns true and the message is ignored.

So on R3, the PONG from R0 is ignored. That means R3 doesn't go through the `clusterMoveNodeSlots` path. R3 already owns the slots because it took them during the failover process.

So the main issue is on other observer nodes (like R1, R2, R4, R5). When they receive R0's PONG, they call `clusterMoveNodeSlots(R0, R3)` which moves slots but doesn't update migration states. Then when R3's PING arrives, the migration states are not updated because the slots already belong to R3.

Let me now create a script to reproduce the issue

  4941	    clusterUpdateState();

I see - the migration states are only shown for the MYSELF node (line 6210). For other nodes, only the slot ranges are shown. So the `get_open_slots` function in the test gets the migration states from a node's own CLUSTER NODES output. Each node reports its own migration states.

So for the test "Migration source is auto-updated after failover in source shard":
- R0 (now replica) should show `[609->-$R1_id]` (migrating to R1)
- R1 (target) should show `[609-<-$R3_id]` (importing from R3, the new source primary)
- R3 (new primary) should show `[609->-$R1_id]` (migrating to R1)
- R4 (replica of R1) should show `[609-<-$R3_id]` (importing from R3)

Now, the question is: how does each node update its migration states?

For R0: R0 originally set `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`. When R0 becomes a replica (via failover), `clusterSetPrimary` is called with `closeSlots=0` (same shard), so `clusterCloseAllSlots()` is NOT called. R0 retains its `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`. So R0 should still show the migrating state. Good.

For R1: R1 originally set `importing_slots_from[609] = R0`. When R1 receives notification that R0 is now a replica and R3 is the new primary, R1 needs to update `importing_slots_from[609]` to point to R3 (the new source primary). This update happens in `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` (lines 2732-2752). But as I analyzed earlier, if `clusterMoveNodeSlots` is called first (from R0's PONG), the slot already belongs to R3 when `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` is called later (from R3's PING), so the migration state update is skipped.

But wait, on R1, does the code path at line 3666-3682 execute? R1 receives PONG from R0. R0 says it's a replica. `sender_claimed_primary` is R3. For R1, `nodeIsReplica(R3)` depends on whether R1 has already recognized R3 as primary. If R1 receives R0's PONG before R3's PING, then R1 still sees R3 as a replica. So `nodeIsReplica(sender_claimed_primary)` is true, and `clusterMoveNodeSlots(R0, R3)` is called. This moves slot 609 from R0 to R3 on R1. But R1's `importing_slots_from[609]` still points to R0.

Then when R3's PING arrives, `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith(R3, ...)` is called. But slot 609 already belongs to R3, so the migration state update is skipped.

However, if R1 receives R3's PING before R0's PONG, then `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith(R3, ...)` is called first. At that point, slot 609 still belongs to R0 (or is unassigned? Actually, R1 still thinks R0 owns slot 609). So the condition at line 2685 (`server.cluster->slots[j] == sender`) is false. The code at lines 2693-2757 runs, which includes updating `importing_slots_from[609]` from R0 to R3 (since R3 is in the same shard as R0). Then later when R0's PONG arrives, `clusterMoveNodeSlots` would try to move slots from R0 to R3, but slot 609 already belongs to R3 (moved by `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith`), so nothing happens.

So the order matters! If R0's PONG arrives before R3's PING, the migration state update is lost. If R3's PING arrives first, it works correctly.

This is a classic race condition. The fix should ensure that migration states are properly updated regardless of message order.

Now, let me think about the proper fix. There are several options:

1. In `clusterMoveNodeSlots`, also update migration states.
2. In the code block that calls `clusterMoveNodeSlots`, update migration states after moving slots.
3. In `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith`, also handle migration state updates when the slot already belongs to the sender.

I think option 3 is the most robust because it ensures migration states are always updated correctly when slot ownership changes, regardless of whether the slot was already moved.

But wait, there's a reason the code at line 2685 just continues: if the slot already belongs to the sender, there's nothing to update. However, the migration/importing states might need updating even if the slot ownership hasn't changed. For example, if the slot was already moved to the new primary (by a previous message), but the importing state still points to the old primary, we need to update it.

Actually, looking at the code more carefully, I think the issue is specifically in the `clusterMoveNodeSlots` function or its caller. The function moves slots but doesn't update migration states. The fix should be to update migration states when slots are moved.

Let me look at what the proper update should be:

When `clusterMoveNodeSlots` moves a slot from `from_node` to `to_node` (where `to_node` is the new primary in the same shard):
1. If `importing_slots_from[slot]` == `from_node`, update it to `to_node`.
2. If `migrating_slots_to[slot]` == `from_node`, update it to `to_node`.

Wait, but `migrating_slots_to` points to the target of migration, not the source. If we're migrating slot 609 TO node X, then `migrating_slots_to[609] = X`. So if `from_node` (old primary) was the migration target, then `migrating_slots_to[609]` would be `from_node`. But that's the case where the migration target had a failover, which is handled by the `else` branch in `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` (lines 2775-2784).

Actually, the case here is different: `from_node` is the source of migration (R0), and we're moving its slots to `to_node` (R3). The observer node (R1) has `importing_slots_from[609] = R0` (importing from the old source). This should be updated to `importing_slots_from[609] = R3` (importing from the new source).

But also, what if the observer node has `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1` (migrating to R1)? That wouldn't be affected because the migration target hasn't changed. However, if the observer node has `migrating_slots_to[609] = R0` (migrating to R0, the old primary), then it should be updated to `migrating_slots_to[609] = R3` (migrating to R3, the new primary).

So the update should be: for each slot moved, if `importing_slots_from[slot]` or `migrating_slots_to[slot]` points to `from_node`, update it to `to_node`.

2026-05-28 18:47:07,557 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
I see! The CLUSTER SETSLOT command is propagated to replicas (line 7013: `forceCommandPropagation(c, PROPAGATE_REPL)`). So when R0 executes `CLUSTER SETSLOT 609 MIGRATING $R1_id`, this command is replicated to R3 (R0's replica). So R3 also sets `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`. That's how R3 gets the migration state.

Similarly, when R1 executes `CLUSTER SETSLOT 609 IMPORTING $R0_id`, this is replicated to R4 (R1's replica). So R4 also sets `importing_slots_from[609] = R0`.

Now, after the failover, R3 becomes the new primary. R3 already has `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1` (because it was replicated from R0). So R3 doesn't need to inherit anything; it already has the migration state.

But what about R1's `importing_slots_from[609]`? R1 originally set it to R0. After the failover, R1 needs to update it to R3 (the new source primary). This update should happen in `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` when R1 receives R3's PING. But as I analyzed, if R0's PONG arrives first and `clusterMoveNodeSlots` moves slots from R0 to R3, then the subsequent `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` call for R3 skips the migration state update.

So the problem is on R1 (and R4, via replication from R1). R1 needs to update `importing_slots_from[609]` from R0 to R3.

Now, let me also consider: does R0's PONG cause `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` to be called? No, because R0 claims to be a replica (not primary). The condition at line 3767 requires `sender_claims_to_be_primary`. So `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` is NOT called for R0's PONG. The slot movement happens via `clusterMoveNodeSlots` directly, bypassing `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith`.

So the fix should be: after `clusterMoveNodeSlots` moves slots from `sender` to `sender_claimed_primary`, we should also update the migration states. Specifically, for each moved slot:
- If `importing_slots_from[slot]` == `sender`, update to `sender_claimed_primary`.
- If `migrating_slots_to[slot]` == `sender`, update to `sender_claimed_primary`.

But also, I should check if there's another scenario: what if the observer node has `migrating_slots_to[slot]` pointing to some node that is in the same shard as `sender`? The code in `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` handles this in the `else` branch (lines 2775-2784). But that code runs when the sender does NOT claim the slot. In our case, the sender (new primary) DOES claim the slot, so that code doesn't run. But if the migration target (not source) had a failover, that would be handled by the else branch.

Actually, wait. Let me re-examine the flow. In the test "Migration source is auto-updated after failover in source shard":
- R0 is migrating slot 609 to R1. So R0 has `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`.
- R1 is importing slot 609 from R0. So R1 has `importing_slots_from[609] = R0`.
- R0 fails, R3 takes over.
- On R1 (the observer), when R1 receives R0's PONG:
  - `sender` = R0 (old primary, now replica)
  - `sender_claimed_primary` = R3 (new primary)
  - `nodeIsReplica(sender_claimed_primary)` = true (R1 hasn't yet recognized R3 as primary)
  - `clusterMoveNodeSlots(R0, R3)` moves slot 609 from R0 to R3
  - But `importing_slots_from[609]` still = R0 (should be R3)
  - `migrating_slots_to[609]` = R1 (unchanged, correct)

So the fix should update `importing_slots_from[609]` from R0 to R3.

Also, what about the case where the observer node has `migrating_slots_to[slot]` = `sender`? That would mean the observer is migrating a slot TO the old primary. Since the old primary is now a replica, the migration should be redirected to the new primary. This is handled by updating `migrating_slots_to[slot]` from `sender` to `sender_claimed_primary`.

But wait, there's also the case where the observer node has `migrating_slots_to[slot]` pointing to some other node in the same shard as `sender`. That case is handled by the `else` branch in `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` (lines 2775-2784), which runs when the sender does NOT claim the slot. But in our scenario, the sender (new primary) DOES claim the slot. However, `migrating_slots_to[slot]` could be pointing to a different node (the migration target), not the sender. So this case is not relevant here.

Let me now implement the fix. I'll modify the code after `clusterMoveNodeSlots` to update migration states.

int clusterMoveNodeSlots(clusterNode *from_node, clusterNode *to_node) {

 *
 * Iterates over all cluster slots, transferring each slot covered
 * by `from_node` to `to_node`. Counts and returns the number of
 * slots transferred.
 *
 * Additionally, updates the migrating/importing states for the
 * transferred slots to point to `to_node` instead of `from_node`. */
int clusterMoveNodeSlots(clusterNode *from_node, clusterNode *to_node) {
    int processed = 0;
    for (int j = 0; j < CLUSTER_SLOTS; j++) {
        if (clusterNodeCoversSlot(from_node, j)) {
            clusterDelSlot(j);
            clusterAddSlot(to_node, j);
            processed++;
            /* Update migration states: if a slot was being imported from or
             * migrated to `from_node`, it should now point to `to_node`. */

            }
            if (server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] == from_node) {
                server.cluster->migrating_slots_to[j] = to_node;
            }
        }
    }
    return processed;

5. For slot 609: `bitmapTestBit(hdr->myslots, 609)` is true (R3 claims it).
6. `server.cluster->slots[609] == R3`? Initially, `server.cluster->slots[609]` is R0. So false.
7. At line 2693: `server.cluster->slots[609]->configEpoch < senderConfigEpoch`? R0's epoch < R3's epoch? Probably true. So we enter the block.
8. At lines 2732-2752: `importing_slots_from[609]` is R0 (not NULL). `importing_slots_from[609] != R3`? R0 != R3, true. `areInSameShard(R3, importing_slots_from[609])`? R3 and R0 are in the same shard, true. So `importing_slots_from[609] = R3`. This updates the importing source from R0 to R3!
9. At lines 2715-2728: `migrating_slots_to[609]` is NULL (R1 doesn't have migrating state for this slot). So nothing.
10. Then at lines 2754-2755: `clusterDelSlot(609); clusterAddSlot(R3, 609);` Slot ownership moves from R0 to R3.

So if R3's PING arrives first, everything works correctly.

But what if R0's PONG arrives before R3's PING?

On R1 (observer), when R0's PONG arrives:
- `sender` = R0 (now replica)
- `sender_claimed_primary` = R3
- `nodeIsReplica(R3)`? R1 hasn't seen R3 as primary yet, so R3 might still be seen as a replica. If so, `clusterMoveNodeSlots(R0, R3)` is called, moving slot 609 from R0 to R3.
- But `importing_slots_from[609]` is still R0 (should be R3).
- Then when R3's PING arrives later: `server.cluster->slots[609] == R3` (already moved). So the condition at line 2685 is true, and it just continues without updating migration states.
- So `importing_slots_from[609]` remains R0, which is wrong.

My fix addresses this by updating `importing_slots_from` in `clusterMoveNodeSlots`. But I also need to consider: what if the migration states need to be updated differently? For example, what if `importing_slots_from[609]` pointed to some node other than `from_node`? That shouldn't happen because the only node that would have `importing_slots_from[609]` set is the migration target (R1), and it points to the source (R0 = from_node). So updating from `from_node` to `to_node` is correct.

But what about `migrating_slots_to`? On R1 (the migration target), `migrating_slots_to[609]` is NULL. On R0 (the source), `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1`. On R3 (new source), `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1` (replicated from R0). On other nodes, `migrating_slots_to[609]` is NULL.

So when `clusterMoveNodeSlots(R0, R3)` is called on an observer node (like R2 or R5), `migrating_slots_to[609]` is NULL, so nothing to update. When it's called on R1, `migrating_slots_to[609]` is NULL. So the `migrating_slots_to` update in my fix is harmless (no false positives).

But wait, what if an observer node has `migrating_slots_to[609]` pointing to `from_node`? That would mean the observer is migrating slot 609 TO `from_node`. If `from_node` is now a replica, the migration should be redirected to `to_node`. My fix handles this case.

Now, I'm thinking about another potential issue: what if `clusterMoveNodeSlots` is called but the sender and sender_claimed_primary are the same? Looking at the code:
```c
serverAssert(sender_claimed_primary->replicaof == sender);
```
So `sender_claimed_primary` is a replica of `sender`. They're different nodes.

Also, what if there are multiple slots being moved, and some have migration states pointing to `from_node` while others don't? My fix iterates over each moved slot and updates only those with matching migration states. That's correct.

Let me also check if there's an issue with the `else` branch at line 3684-3695. When `sender` moves to a different shard, `clusterDelNodeSlots(sender)` is called. But migration states pointing to `sender` are not cleared. This could be a separate issue, but it's not related to the PR description.

Now, I'm reasonably confident that my fix addresses the race condition. But I want to make sure there aren't other code paths that have the same issue.

Let me also check the `clusterProcessPacket` code for the case where `sender_claimed_primary` is NOT a replica (i.e., already recognized as primary). In that case, the code doesn't call `clusterMoveNodeSlots`. But the slots still need to be moved from `sender` to `sender_claimed_primary`. Who does that?

If `sender_claimed_primary` is already a primary, it means that `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith` was already called with `sender_claimed_primary` as sender. In that call, the slots were already moved from the old owner to `sender_claimed_primary`. So when `sender` (old primary) later announces it's a replica, the slots are already with `sender_claimed_primary`. So no additional slot movement is needed.

But wait, what if `sender_claimed_primary` was already a primary for a different reason (e.g., it was already a primary before the failover)? That's not possible because `sender_claimed_primary` was previously a replica of `sender` (asserted at line 3667: `serverAssert(sender_claimed_primary->replicaof == sender)`). So `sender_claimed_primary` was definitely a replica before the failover.

So the only way `sender_claimed_primary` is not a replica is if it has already been updated to primary by a previous message (e.g., R3's PING arrived before R0's PONG). In that case, the slots were already moved by `clusterUpdateSlotsConfigWith`, which properly handles migration states.

So my fix covers the remaining case where R0's PONG arrives first.

Let me now also think about another edge case: what if the observer node is the new primary itself (R3) and it receives R0's PONG? As I analyzed earlier, `nodeIsReplica(R3)` is false on R3, so the `clusterMoveNodeSlots` path is not taken. But does R3 need to update any migration states? R3 already has `migrating_slots_to[609] = R1` from replication. R3 doesn't have `importing_slots_from[609]` set. So R3 is fine.

Now, let me run the full test suite for slot migration to ensure nothing is broken:

> [test-failure] Slot-migration related
> ```
> *** Migration source is auto-updated after failover in source shard
> *** Replica redirects key access in migrating slots
> *** Replica of migrating node returns ASK redirect after READONLY
> *** Replica of migrating node returns TRYAGAIN after READONLY
> *** Replica of importing node returns TRYAGAIN after READONLY and ASKING
> *** New replica inherits migrating slot
> *** New replica inherits importing slot
> ```
> 
> These tests seems to be consistently failing in the daily runs.
> 
> I tried to narrow down the commit https://github.com/valkey-io/valkey/pull/2301 that might possibly cause this.
> 
> I have tested this by reverting this commit on my personal repo and found the tests not failing

The tests listed are:
1. Migration source is auto-updated after failover in source shard
2. Replica redirects key access in migrating slots
3. Replica of migrating node returns ASK redirect after READONLY
4. Replica of migrating node returns TRYAGAIN after READONLY
5. Replica of importing node returns TRYAGAIN after READONLY and ASKING
6. New replica inherits migrating slot
7. New replica inherits importing slot

Tests 2-5 are about client commands (GET, MGET) being redirected correctly during migration. These tests depend on the migration states being correct. If migration states are inconsistent, the redirect behavior would be wrong.

For example, test "Replica redirects key access in migrating slots":
```tcl
test "Replica redirects key access in migrating slots" {
    assert_equal [get_open_slots 0] "\[609->-$R1_id\]"
    assert_equal [get_open_slots 1] "\[609-<-$R0_id\]"
    assert_equal [get_open_slots 3] "\[609->-$R1_id\]"
    assert_equal [get_open_slots 4] "\[609-<-$R0_id\]"
    catch {[R 3 get aga]} e
    set port0 [srv 0 port]
    assert_equal "MOVED 609 127.0.0.1:$port0" $e
}
```

This test expects that R3 (replica of R0) returns MOVED to R0 (the primary) for a key in the migrating slot. This is because the replica knows the slot is being migrated and redirects to the primary.

If the migration state on R3 is wrong (e.g., `migrating_slots_to[609]` is not set), R3 might return a different redirect or try to serve the key locally, which would fail the test.

My fix ensures that when slots are moved from the old primary to the new primary, the migration states are updated accordingly. This should keep the migration states consistent and prevent these tests from failing.

But wait, tests 2-5 are run BEFORE the failover! Look at the test order:
1. "Slot migration states are replicated"
2. "Migration target is auto-updated after failover in target shard"
3. "Migration source is auto-updated after failover in source shard"  <-- failover happens
4. "Replica redirects key access in migrating slots"  <-- after failover, but R0 restored as primary
5. "Replica of migrating node returns ASK redirect after READONLY"
6. "Replica of migrating node returns TRYAGAIN after READONLY"
7. "Replica of importing node returns TRYAGAIN after READONLY and ASKING"
8. "New replica inherits migrating slot"
9. "New replica inherits importing slot"

Test 3 triggers a failover and then restores R0 as primary. Tests 4-7 run after the failover and restoration. So tests 4-7 depend on the migration states being correct after the failover and restoration.

If the failover in test 3 causes migration states to be incorrectly updated (or not updated), then tests 4-7 would fail. My fix addresses this by ensuring migration states are properly updated during the failover.

But what about tests 8-9? These tests reset replicas and rejoin them. They expect the new replicas to inherit the migration states. If the migration states on the primary are wrong (due to the failover), the new replicas would inherit wrong states. My fix should help here too.

Now, I'm fairly confident that my fix addresses the issue. But let me also consider: could there be another issue related to the `serverAssert(sender->numslots == 0)` that was added by #2301? If this assert fails, the server would crash. But the tests would show a crash, not a test failure. The PR description mentions test failures, not crashes. So the assert is probably not the issue.

Wait, but maybe the assert could cause a crash in some edge case? Let me check: `sender->numslots` is the number of slots owned by `sender`. After `clusterMoveNodeSlots` moves all slots from `sender` to `sender_claimed_primary`, `sender->numslots` should be 0. But what if `sender` also had some slots that were not moved? `clusterMoveNodeSlots` iterates over all slots and moves those covered by `sender`. So all slots should be moved. The assert should hold.

But what if `sender` had 0 slots to begin with? Then `clusterMoveNodeSlots` returns 0, and the assert still holds (0 == 0). That's fine.

So the assert is not the issue.

I think my fix is complete. Let me submit it.
